After the New President is Elected

French Cabinet Submits Resignation 83

Herriot to Organize New Cabinet; Theidier Agreed to Serve Temporarily ▲ Guomin News Agency, Versailles, 11th. After Lebrun was elected the new French President today, Theidier immediately submitted the cabinet's general resignation, but agreed to continue serving as before until the new Chamber of Deputies opens its inaugural meeting on June 1st and Herriot organizes a new cabinet, then hand over. ▲ Havas, Paris, 10th. Theidier stated in his letter of resignation that (the cabinet hereby resigns to the President, according to customary practice, the new President assumes office at the beginning, and the cabinet resigns, the new President must reappoint the resigning members. This time, I hope the President will not adhere to the precedents, because the current responsibilities are heavy and difficult to deal with. Various important negotiations are underway, and important decisions that affect the future must be taken almost every day. In order to assume this kind of responsibility, it must be possible to act freely. However, the results of the recent elections have changed the majority party in the Chamber of Deputies. Therefore, the current cabinet has lost its freedom of action and must ask the President to break the precedent. As for routine affairs, the cabinet members still obey the order and are willing to temporarily take charge, but for the sake of the overall situation, I hope to unload this burden soon.) ▲ Reuters, Paris, 10th. After Lebrun was elected President of France, the current Prime Minister Theidier immediately resigned to the new President in accordance with French political precedent. The government party led by Theidier failed in this election, so his resignation should be approved. The first task of the new President is to instruct the leaders of other parties to organize a cabinet. Although Lebrun's election was expected, people from all walks of life still gathered in Versailles on the day of the election to be the first to receive the announcement. However, because the former President was assassinated, the whole country mourned, resulting in a less enthusiastic atmosphere than in previous presidential elections. The joint vote of the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies had black紗覆蓋 on the ballot box. Lebrun, in his capacity as Speaker of the Senate, announced the opening of the meeting, saying, (The President has passed away suddenly.) As soon as these words were uttered, all the councilors stood up in respect. Lebrun, representing the Congress, paid tribute to Doumer's portrait, and then read a speech, the main idea of which was to express sympathy to Doumer's family. As a result of the election, Lebrun won 633 votes out of 826 votes, and was elected with a large majority. After the election, the inauguration ceremony was held. Prime Minister Theidier supervised the inauguration and personally handed over the election announcement documents and the national seal to the new President. The exact number of votes in this election is as follows: Lebrun 633 votes, Paul Faure 114 votes, Painleve 12 votes, Cachin 8 votes, other candidates received a total of 10 votes, blank and invalid votes 49 votes. ▲ Guomin News Agency, Versailles, 11th. It is reported that before being elected the new French President this morning, Lebrun had received three threatening letters. One letter was signed by a Russian terrorist, and the content of all three letters was to threaten him that if he was elected, he would suffer the same fate as Doumer. Therefore, the police were heavily guarded today, but it is expected that these letters were written by madmen.

Manuscript of Assassin Donated to German Publishing House 84

Pre-Prepared Will; Confession of Self ▲ Guomin News Agency, Berlin, 10th. A large publishing house in Berlin received a large package from Paris today. The package was sent by Gokulov, the murderer of French President Doumer, from Paris on the day of the assassination. It contained his own will, confession, and a novel he wrote. Inside the package, there was also a letter stating that the book was Gokulov's masterpiece and he believed it would be popular for a while. He has donated all the copyrights to the publishing house, but the publishing house should provide 50% of the profits to his wife for her lifelong living expenses. The publishing house has now accepted these terms and has hired someone to translate the Russian work. The book is originally named (Cossack Romance). The first part is almost entirely the history of one person, and the background is pre-war Russia. The second part, called (Adult), narrates post-war Russia. Throughout the whole book, there is an anti-Soviet meaning. The other will and self-confession have been sent by the publishing house to the French police authorities. Great Disturbance in the German Congress

National Socialist Party Shows Its Power 85

Severely Questioning the Impropriety of Suppressing the Stormtroopers; Financial Bill Finally Passed Second Reading ▲ Guomin News Agency, Berlin, 10th. After the German Congress convened today, as expected, it became a scene of verbal battles and hand-to-hand combat.

Goring, the leader of the National Socialist Party, strongly defended the no-confidence motion proposed by the party, while Groner, the Minister of Defense and Interior Minister, tried his best to defend the legitimacy of the government's disbanding of the National Socialist Party Stormtroopers. The two sides could not avoid verbal conflict, which quickly caused an uproar in the whole hall, causing the meeting to rest for ten minutes before it could continue. However, at the beginning of the meeting, the venue was still relatively quiet. First, the second reading of the government's proposed fund bill was passed by 245 votes to 224 votes. All members of the National Socialist Party, the Communist Party, the National Rights Party, and several other small parties voted against the government. After the bill was voted on, Strasser, a key figure in the National Socialist Party, stepped onto the podium to explain the party's economic plan, and the audience listened attentively. After that, Goring, the leader of the party, stepped onto the podium to question the government's suppression of the National Socialist Party Stormtroopers, his tone was extremely fierce, demanding the revocation of the emergency order to disband the team, claiming that this ban was due to foreign pressure. At this time, Prime Minister Brüning stood up to deny, stressing that the ban was issued purely for internal political reasons, and that the government would never succumb to foreign pressure. At this time, members of the National Socialist Party issued jeers, and the noise started, becoming more and more intense. Vice-President Eisele repeatedly asked members to maintain order, and the meeting was able to continue. Lithuanian Pan-Nationalist Party

Public Telegrams 94

From Xi'an to the Shen Bao: We, the residents of Shaanxi, have suffered from years of continuous disasters, with deaths reported everywhere. Thanks to your repeated assistance, we have managed to survive. However, rural areas are bankrupt, and there are still many unemployed. Even without various disasters this year, the survivors in the disaster areas would still find it difficult to make a living. Unexpectedly, spring brought successive severe frosts, wind, and hailstorms, coupled with months of severe drought without rain, causing crops to wither and creating a tragic situation all around. Moreover, in various districts north of the Wei River and in counties along the western route, many fields have not been sown, making harvest hopeless. People are demolishing houses and fleeing, reporting disasters and requesting relief in nearly seventy counties. Relief efforts are inadequate, leaving us deeply ashamed and heartbroken. We would rather face death than bear this. We earnestly beseech you to show great compassion, quickly extend a helping hand to thoroughly save the remaining people, and widely bestow your magnanimous grace. It is the way of a gentleman to help those in urgent need, and the way of a bodhisattva to give charity. The telegram is urgent, and we cannot help but weep in prayer. Kang Yuyao, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Relief Association, bows in reverence.

From Fuzhou to the Shen Bao, forwarded to all newspapers and compatriots nationwide: The Sino-Japanese Shanghai Ceasefire Agreement was formally signed on the 5th, the harm of which to the nation is unparalleled. According to the terms of the agreement, our troops lose the ability to mobilize within our own territory, while Japanese troops can be stationed in our interior. As for security, it is entirely maintained by police commanded by a joint committee. Moreover, there is no clear stipulation regarding the so-called temporary restrictions. How can we be sure that our government authorities, who do not consider the people as important, will not cause confusion or reversal in the details, or that there are no other secret clauses besides the five items? The secret treaty of 1905 gave the Japanese a pretext, and the Shanghai Agreement of 1932 is even more unfathomable. The 19th Route Army is exhausted and without reinforcements. The entire populace feels immense pain. Yet the government willingly bends the knee and speaks humbly. The imperialists' division and slaughter are gradually being revealed. The state exists to protect the people, and the people love the country. Survival and demise are interdependent and closely linked. What our hearts perceive as dangerous, how can we remain silent? We vow to deny these conditions that are detrimental to the people and will not stop until the goal of their cancellation is achieved. We hope our compatriots will rise up and pursue this urgently. The interests of the people must not be exploited. This is our heartfelt plea, submitted for your public review. The Joint Conference of Student Representatives from Secondary and Higher Education Institutions in Fuzhou bows in reverence.

Important News 95

The Fourth Meeting of the National Government 96

Luoyang dispatch: The National Government Committee held its fourth meeting at the National Government on the 10th. Attendees included Wang Zhengting, Liu Shouchong, Enkebatu, and Chairman Lin Sen. The following matters were discussed: 1. Resolved to announce the Enforcement Law of the Civil Procedure Law. 2. Resolved to announce the Organizational Regulations of the National Bureau of Weights and Measures of the Ministry of Industry. 3. Resolved to announce the Organizational Regulations of the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee. 4. The Central Executive Committee sent a letter stating that at the Second Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee, members Wang Zhaoming and Ju Zheng proposed pensions for deceased and disabled soldiers over the years, and member Feng Yuxiang proposed honoring martyrs and providing pensions for the disabled. The Second Plenary Session resolved to hand these cases over to the National Government to establish a Pensions Committee for handling. It was resolved to forward the case to the Executive Yuan for instructions to the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Interior for joint consultation and handling. 5. Member Kong Xiangxi telegraphed to request a clarification of six points regarding internal affairs: (1) The regulations for punishing bandits and kidnappers should not be abolished. (2) The positions of administrative officials should be better protected. (3) Judges should not be replaced lightly. (4) County magistrates should be selected based on their talents and given real power, and their authority should not be distributed to various bureaus. (5) In the execution of provincial administration, responsibility lies with the various departments. The secretariat of the provincial government should not establish sections similar in function to the various departments, to avoid delays in submission and division of authority. (6) A salary sufficient to maintain integrity is a permanent principle of the state. In recent years, salaries have been reduced due to internal and external troubles, which was a temporary measure that could not be helped. However, if officials are not adequately supported, it will be difficult for them to serve the public with an empty stomach. It seems that this should not be taken as a regular practice. It was resolved to forward the case to the Executive Yuan. (6) The Executive Yuan presented a report from the Ministry of Industry requesting that the deadlines for stock transfer procedures in the Enforcement Law of the Company Law be extended by one year each. The Executive Yuan passed the proposal and requested approval for record, in addition to instructions. It was resolved to approve the record. (7) The Executive Yuan presented a report stating that at the 22nd meeting of the Executive Yuan, Minister of Education Zhu Jiahua proposed that the Compilation and Examination Department of the ministry be abolished and a National Compilation and Translation Bureau be established. The organizational regulations and regular and temporary budget estimates were drafted and submitted for public decision. It was resolved to approve the proposal. In addition to ordering the ministry to announce and implement these regulations through a ministry order and to send the regular and temporary budget estimates to the Accounting Office of the National Government for review and transfer to the Central Political Council for approval, the document was submitted for review and record. It was resolved to approve the record.

Japanese 101

Sailors Trapped in Poverty 102

▲7,000 Sailors Nationwide are Unemployed The Kobe Shimbun reported that the future of the maritime industry is bleak and there is no hope of recovery. Currently, sailors nationwide are trapped in an unprecedented state of poverty. There are 3,830 ordinary sailors and 2,621 senior officers. If all of them were employed, with 34 ordinary sailors per 5,000-ton vessel, that would require 650,000 tons of shipping. With an average of eight senior officers per vessel, that would require 1,635,000 tons of shipping. Currently, about 560 senior officers graduate from merchant marine academies nationwide each year. Not only is there no room for senior officers, but it is also extremely difficult for sailors, firemen, oilers, etc., to find jobs. Currently, the principals of various local merchant marine academies are holding important meetings to study solutions.

He Chengjun Publishes 104

Disaster Relief and Bandit Suppression Propositions 105

▲Disaster relief is more important than bandit suppression ▲But disaster relief must proceed in tandem with bandit suppression A Hankou dispatch states that He Chengjun, the Pacification Commissioner stationed in Hubei, published a statement on disaster relief and bandit suppression on the 10th, saying: "Although disaster relief and bandit suppression are two separate matters, they are actually inseparable. In the current situation, disaster relief is even more important than bandit suppression. Since the floods last year, people have been displaced. Although the central and local governments have tried to provide relief, the disaster area is too large, and there are too many victims. Relief efforts are insufficient, and funds and wheat are difficult to sustain. Moreover, since the September 18th Incident, affected by the national crisis, the various charitable relief efforts have ended long ago, American wheat has been exhausted, and there are no funds left. Previously, there was still hope for the spring harvest, but now the disaster area has not recovered, and planting has been missed. If there is no harvest this year, the restoration of the disaster area to its original state is almost impossible. Thinking of the millions of victims who have no clothes or food, it is truly pitiful. If we do not urgently seek relief, the livelihoods of the starving people will be in jeopardy, which will affect military operations for bandit suppression. For example, when Army Commander Xu Kecheng (i.e., Xu Yuanquan) was in Yingcheng directing bandit suppression, he personally witnessed the suffering of the disaster victims and privately disbursed 4,000 bags of flour. This shows the large number of disaster victims in the bandit areas. I also recall that before the flood last year, He's bandits were defeated at Wudang Mountain, and there were fewer than 10,000 remaining. Duan's bandits numbered only 3,000 to 4,000. Due to the flood, they could not be completely wiped out at that time. In less than a year, He has gathered more than 10,000 again. It is inevitable that hungry people will be forced by hunger and cold and enticed by bandits. How can hungry people willingly become bandits? If there is adequate relief, they will naturally awaken and return to good. Therefore, if bandit suppression does not urgently seek disaster relief, it may be difficult to achieve success on time. People from all walks of life are aware of this situation. In order to find ways to provide relief to the people in the bandit areas, I have consulted with Chairman Xia Lingbing (i.e., Xia Douyin) and requested that Zhu Huaibing, the director of the Civil Affairs Department, go to the counties along the Nang River to inspect, comfort the refugees, and restore their livelihoods. Yesterday, Director Zhu telegraphed to report that he had arrived in Hanchuan and said that disaster victims were everywhere, which was truly heartbreaking. Yesterday, the Flood Relief Association勉凑10,000 yuan amidst great difficulties to remit for relief. Therefore, while bandit suppression is an urgent task at present, providing relief to disaster victims is even more urgent. I have already stated this to Chairman Chiang and Premier Wang in Beijing, and they both clearly understand and are willing to find ways to provide relief. At that time, the Shanghai War broke out, and the national crisis was urgent, so the government was unable to take care of everything. Now the central finances are still extremely difficult. The Flood Relief Association recently telegraphed the central government, requesting that it borrow 20 million tons of American wheat for Hubei Province, as before, which will be repaid by Hubei Province in the future, but no reply has been received yet, and it is not known whether it can be done. In short, disaster relief is the most important plan at present. How to raise huge sums of money and provide relief as soon as possible is what I hope people from all walks of life will pay close attention to. As for the bandit suppression situation, it has been good recently. Since the battles of Wamiaoji and Longquan Town in central Hubei, the remnants of He and Duan's bandits have been severely wounded, and the bandit forces have been greatly reduced. The remnants are fleeing in all directions and are being cleared out by the troops of Xiao Zhichu and Zhang Zhenhan of the 10th Army. The remnants of Diaowen Lake will also be eliminated soon. Supervisor Xu Kecheng is planning and directing military operations for bandit suppression in that area and will go to Beijing again in a few days to meet with Chairman Chiang and report everything. As for eastern Hubei, Zhang Yinxiang, Ge Yunlong, Peng Zhenshan, and other troops are stationed for suppression. The Pinghan Railway line in northern Hubei is garrisoned by Ma Hongkui, Fan Shisheng, and other troops, as well as the 13th Division, and it is very peaceful. The remnants of Kong Hechong's bandits in Daye and Yangxin in southern Hubei, bordering Jiangxi, are being cleared out by Guo Rudong, Xie Bin, and the security regiments, and the fighting is still fierce. However, the funds for bandit suppression are difficult to obtain and urgently need to be raised. The local gentry of this province have previously established a Clean-up Promotion Association to assist the government in its work, but the gentry and wealthy donations have not yet yielded any results. Currently, the Hubei Salt Affairs Audit Office has agreed to assist with 100,000 yuan per month for a period of nine months to be allocated to the Hubei Provincial Bandit Suppression Fund. The office has telegraphed the Shanghai General Audit Office to negotiate, but it is still hoped that 150,000 yuan can be allocated per month and the period extended to one year. As for the expenses of the National Army stationed in Hubei, after my earnest request to Chairman Chiang, the monthly payment has been increased by 10%, but it is still only enough for the troops' food. After the troops are mobilized, straw sandals and porters are needed, and funds are needed everywhere. Hubei Province should bear 420,000 yuan for bandit suppression expenses, and although the provincial treasury is stretched, it will still find ways to allocate it to meet urgent needs. I have already sent a letter to Chairman Xia, instructing the Finance Department to include this in the necessary items of administrative expenses and pay it first, and then reimburse it after the Clean-up Promotion Association raises funds. In addition, after Division Commander Wang Lingji arrived in Hankou, he discussed specific measures for clearing out the bandits in western Hubei and assisting in clearing out the remnants of bandits in central Hubei, and there will be results in the near future. In short, disaster relief must proceed in tandem with bandit suppression, and bandit suppression must have sufficient funding. He is discussing this in detail with Chairman Xia and all parties these days, and we must proceed simultaneously." (May 10th)

Wuxi 110

▲Recruitment of Female Workers Causes Turmoil Gan Jian Silk Factory, located under the Gongyun Bridge, posted recruitment conditions for new female workers on the 2nd of this month, stipulating that female workers with beautiful appearance, fashionable dress, and no pregnancy or children would be recruited into the factory. On the 4th, eight machines were started first. Upon hearing this news, the old female workers rose up in opposition and appealed to the Party and government agencies for assistance. Yesterday (the 9th) at 6:00 a.m., more than 200 old female workers, driven by livelihood concerns, all took the initiative to enter the factory to work. Seeing this, the factory, fearing trouble, reported to the 4th Detachment of the Business Corps. Upon receiving the report, the detachment immediately sent more than ten members, armed with guns, to suppress the situation. At that time, there was a loud noise, and people refused to be dissuaded. The Business Corps fired a volley of warning shots into the sky. Fortunately, no one was injured. The situation was tense, and the order was in chaos. After half an hour, the female workers dispersed like frightened birds. The factory owner, Cheng Bingruo, fearing that the turmoil would escalate, immediately suspended work and made proper arrangements for the aftermath.

When his family heard the news and went to save him, he had already died. The old mother in the hall, with her son dying for the country, was in a very tragic state.

Urgent Notice Issued Yesterday 119

▲Water Will Be Shut Off at the End of the Month for Failure to Sign Contracts Under the New Regulations ▲New Houses Cost Five Times More Than Under the Old System ▲Real Estate Association Proposes a Fair Solution The British-owned Shanghai Public Concession Water Company is implementing a water meter system. After setting the price of water meters, the Real Estate Association resolutely opposed collecting it on their behalf, while the tenants opposed increasing the burden. The company issued an urgent notice to all sectors yesterday, stating that if contracts are not signed in accordance with the new regulations, water will be cut off at the end of this month. The Real Estate Association will hold a general meeting on the 14th to discuss how to deal with it and propose a method for installing water meters. The various situations are recorded as follows: ▲Urgent Notice The British-owned Shanghai Water Company issued an urgent notice to all sectors yesterday, which read: "To whom it may concern, because the water supply agreement between our company and your users, which was previously based on a monthly flat rate, will expire on May 31, it is now invalid. We have sent a new contract for water supply calculated according to the water meter. If the new contract is not signed and returned to our company before the expiration date, the supply will be stopped immediately. If you have not received the new contract form that was previously sent, or if you have received it and lost it, please come to our company's general management office to collect a replacement." ▲Proposed Solution The Real Estate Association wrote to the British-owned Shanghai Water Company, saying: "To whom it may concern, we previously received your letter dated December 7, 1931, regarding the installation of water meters. We believe that the matter is of great importance and requires detailed research before expressing our opinions, etc. We have heard about it, and now we will describe our exploration as follows: (1) Your company should pay attention to the following facts. According to the actual rent, 7.5% of the rent is for water, and the monthly water fee is 55 yuan. After installing water meters, the average monthly water fee is 290 yuan. If so, installing water meters will increase the water fee by more than five times compared to the flat-rate system, that is, from 7.5% to 37.5%. If the landlord has to pay this water fee on behalf of the tenant, then the landlord's actual rent for a 100-yuan flat-rate rent is more than 94 yuan, excluding surcharges, while the water meter system is only about 64 yuan. If the increased 30 yuan is transferred to the tenant's direct burden, then wouldn't the tenant who pays 100 yuan for rent, including water fees, have to bear a total of 130 yuan for water fees and rent? And the water fee will account for one-third of the rent, how will users make a living? This is a major problem in Shanghai. (2) The above-mentioned facts are implemented by your company, such as the collection of municipal general losses, and the methods of telephone, natural gas, and electricity are not related to real estate operators, but real estate operators are also water users, and they also have direct interests. Moreover, the common people account for a very large percentage of all users. When this association implements its claims, it has to make a statement on behalf of them, and it does not intend to emulate utilitarians who only seek no harm to themselves, but only transfer their harm to others and do not care. (3) Installing water meters to obtain fairness and save waste is a matter of course. This association absolutely agrees, and the principle of dividing the water rate into two types and taking into account the lives of the common people is even more the principle that modern social policies should have. However, this association believes that the cost and deposit of installing water meters should be borne by the landlord, which is absolutely different from the installation methods of telephones, electricity, and natural gas, and is even more in absolute conflict with legal principles. (4) The following methods should be used for installing water meters: (A) Each household in the existing houses must install one meter, and the cost and deposit should be borne by the user. After installing the water meter, the landlord should remove the water fee from the original flat-rate rent and only collect the actual rent. (B) All matters concerning the installation of water meters for each household in the new houses must be directly negotiated by the water company and the user, and the landlord shall not be responsible for any responsibilities. (5) Regardless of whether water meters are installed or not, all landlords have no obligation to collect or bear the usage fees on behalf of others in accordance with legal principles and the precedents of other public utilities. Before this method can be implemented, in any case, anything that increases the landlord's difficulties and expenses cannot be absolutely agreed. Correspondence is hereby made, and it is hoped that you will investigate accordingly. Postal Workers' Union and Employees' Union

Reaffirming the Plan to Consolidate the Postal Foundation 120

▲Continuing to Submit to the Ministry for Open Adoption ▲Writing to All Sectors to Report the Facts In view of the increase in postage rates and the increased burden on the public, the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and Employees' Union, based on their duty to serve and based on the past facts of the postal service, drafted an outline and reasons for a plan to consolidate the postal foundation, prepared a document and sent representatives to Beijing to make statements to the important organs of the Central National Government, and made more sincere proposals to the Ministry of Communications. They originally hoped to seek a method that would take into account both parties on the principle of national undertakings and the interests of the public, in order to build a great cause for a hundred years. Yesterday, the returning representatives reported that Chen Fumu, Deputy Minister of the Ministry of Communications, expressed that he insisted on his personal position and seemed unwilling to openly and fully adopt the proposed plan. The two associations believe that if the Ministry of Communications does not accept the plan, the future of the postal service will be in great danger, and they unanimously decided to submit it to the Ministry of Communications again, requesting open adoption and immediate implementation, and issued a report to all sectors. The submitted document and the letter to all sectors are recorded below: ▲Submitting to the Ministry to Request Approval of the Plan to Consolidate the Postal Foundation, Lay the Foundation for National Undertakings, Maintain the Interests of the Public, and Pray for Prompt Orders to Follow, in Order to Comfort the Public The members of the association, etc., dedicate themselves to the postal service, deeply aware of the difficulty of creating the postal service and remembering the harshness of the postal environment. Therefore, when the Ministry is implementing an increase in postage rates to expand the postal environment, we especially admire the Ministry's hard work in maintaining the postal service. We have gathered the experience of postal employees across the country who speak about the postal service, compiled the facts of the postal service's past history, analyzed the advantages and disadvantages, and weighed the importance. We have drafted a concrete plan to consolidate the postal foundation, with a total of three outlines and six items, and attached four reasons. The main points are: All postal surpluses should be used to develop the postal service and other necessary purposes, determine the principle of using the postal service to support the postal service, and implement special postal accounting to restore the postal service's economic resources and consolidate the postal service's economic foundation. The current postal service's deficit of four million should be quickly cut down by the Savings and Remittance Bureau and stop subsidies to airlines. The money saved can be gradually used to make up for the deficit. Increasing postage rates is not a fundamental solution to remedy the postal service. Moreover, increasing the burden only causes public criticism. Therefore, please temporarily maintain the original postage rates to maintain the people's faith. After the administrative reform is implemented, if there is a shortage, we will slowly find ways to remedy the economic shortage. Then the public will be able to understand the Ministry's hard work and be happy to bear the burden. This concerns consolidating the postal economy. The postal service's performance is fortunate to be maintained because of the integrity of the administrative system and the guarantee of employment. Therefore, it can maintain its independence and not be shocked by political tides. Since recent years, the postal savings and remittance business has been severely divided. The so-called Savings and Remittance Bureau, which is set up separately, uses the words "postal service," but the actual administrative management and the advancement and retreat of personnel all use the postal service system. It is almost like a corrupt parasitic institution. If the bureau is not quickly cut down and the savings and remittance business is still returned to the Postal General Bureau, and the original organization is merged and handled, then not only will the postal savings and remittance business be completely destroyed, and the people's savings will have no guarantee, but also the postal service's international status will be destroyed. The future of the postal service will be greatly hindered, and it is not just a matter of setting up parasitic institutions, abusing non-postal personnel, and increasing the postal service's huge burden. It is found that our country's transportation undertakings have been repeatedly affected by political tides and have all been damaged. The Ministry has presided over transportation administration, adopted the postal system, and ordered other transportation undertakings to gradually improve, help them develop, and support them forward. It is not possible to destroy the postal system and go with other transportation undertakings, and pull them back. As for how to maintain the independence of postal administration and the personnel treatment system, the plan has detailed them. This concerns consolidating the administration. The postal service's personnel treatment system is the only key factor for the postal service's prosperity. At first, the Ministry temporarily canceled the two-yuan subsidy that was related to the lives of all employees, and recently, we suddenly received the Ministry's Instruction No. 904, which strictly restricted the promotion methods, causing the feelings of the officials to be anxious and uneasy. The Association believes that restricting personnel promotion is to destroy the postal service's good system, and canceling the two-yuan subsidy is to destroy the guarantee of employees' treatment. This measure is contrary to the Ministry's original intention of expanding postal services. The Association cannot agree to it, and has repeatedly listed the reasons in detail in the case. However, after many days, we have not seen a clear order to cancel it. It seems that such repeated delays will not ease the employees. This concerns maintaining the personnel treatment system. The above three concerns are all related to the postal service's centennial plan. If one is missing, the postal service will not be able to stand on its own. Today, the Ministry initially resolutely increased postage rates, and then separately reviewed and reduced them, which shows the Ministry's determination to expand postal services. However, it is only concerned with the symptoms and does not seek the root cause. It is not the way to achieve a great undertaking. The Association is concerned that if postal administration and the economy are not maintained and the postal foundation is consolidated, the benefits of the reduction will be difficult to last, and the resentment of the increase will be gathered. The postal service itself will only become thinner and wither, and will eventually fall into a state of eternal doom. All the employees of the Association are closely related to each other, and they love and care more. They are wandering in five directions, not just for a day or two. For this reason, we risk everything to express our feelings and will not avoid any ministry to implement them. Then more than 30,000 employees will exhaust their minds and blood and will not avoid any difficulties to be the Ministry's backing and promote its realization. If there is further delay, the employees will be motivated by temporary indignation, and their actions may exceed the norm. The Association has the intention to love the postal service, but there is no way to suppress it. We hope that the Ministry will make a decisive decision and issue a clear order to follow it. The plan to consolidate the postal foundation will be implemented immediately, and the promotion restrictions will be canceled and the original two-yuan subsidy will be restored, so as to comfort the public and reassure the people. We cannot wait to be ordered. We respectfully submit this to the Minister and Deputy Minister of the Ministry of Communications. ▲To All Sectors All agencies, people's organizations, and compatriots across the country: Our Chinese postal service, fortunately relying on a strict system, has gradually progressed over the past 30 years and has achieved good results. The society recognizes it as the only remaining transportation undertaking in our country. Later, through the efforts of postal employees across the country, we recovered postal rights and placed them under the management of the National Government's Ministry of Communications. We deeply hoped to vigorously revive and keep pace with Europe and the United States. However, since recent years, rights have been recovered, but the government has been deteriorating. Dividing the business and destroying the system have led to administrative differences and reduced efficiency. Moreover, successive transportation authorities have regarded the postal service as a financial agency and have spared no effort to withdraw postal construction and development funds for non-postal or other non-essential purposes, resulting in decades of painstaking management and the postal service's surplus turning into a deficit. Therefore, the authorities, in order to make up for the postal service's budget deficit, resolutely disregarded the survivors of the disaster and implemented an increase in postage rates, which increased the burden on the public. Alas, who is doing this? Who is causing this? All our compatriots should see this. The Association is deeply concerned about the deterioration of the postal foundation. The drawbacks may not be remedied by increasing the burden on the public. Therefore, we are forced to fulfill our duty to serve the society and based on our loyalty to maintain the undertaking, we have drafted a concrete plan to consolidate the postal foundation, with a total of three outlines and six items, and attached four reasons (the original plan is attached separately). We have already sincerely requested the Ministry of Communications to adopt it, so that it can be exempted from all undue burdens on the postal service, restore the postal service's economic resources, and maintain the integrity of the postal system and the stability of personnel treatment. Then the future of the postal service will gradually move towards brightness, and the order to recover the increase in postage rates, which compatriots from all walks of life have requested to reduce the burden, can be finally realized. The Association is considering the interests of the postal service, the society, the national undertaking, and the compatriots. We are wandering in five directions, not just for a day or two. Now that the postal foundation is in danger, we should gather the strength of the whole country to be the pioneers in consolidating the postal service. We will not avoid the difficulties and toil in order to compensate for the past negligence in maintenance. We hope that all sectors will appreciate our foolish sincerity and encourage us to achieve our goals. With this, we wish you peace and security. Sincerely, Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and Shanghai Postal Employees' Union

The Southeast Medical University Relief Team Concludes 122

When the war clouds were looming in Shanghai a few days ago, Guo Qiyuan, President of Southeast Medical University, rushed to Shanghai from Hubei to summon the school's graduates from all over the country to join the Red Cross and organize the Seventh Relief Team. They went through many dangers and rescued two or three hundred wounded soldiers and civilians. After the Nineteenth Route Army retreated in early March, the team was ordered to go to Kunshan and Suzhou to organize a rear hospital. For the past month, the war has stopped at the front, and all the Red Cross relief teams have been ordered to disband. The Seventh Team was specially ordered to continue working due to its outstanding performance, and to handle the unfinished business of the rear hospital. Yesterday, team members Shen Xunru and others came to Shanghai to tell reporters that Director Guo has ordered all team members to disband automatically in order to conclude the work, because the wounded soldiers in the hospital have all gradually recovered.

Resumption of Business Is Still Undetermined 125

Yesterday, various newspapers carried the news that the Commercial Press would resume business on a regular basis. In order to clarify the truth, the reporter visited a certain official of the press. According to him, this news is completely untrue. The press's main factory was destroyed and shut down. The Hong Kong and Peiping branch factories have not stopped work and have not expanded their scope. As for the building above the Yunfei Motor Company on Jing'an Temple Road in Shanghai, it is temporarily rented by the press to store the remaining machines, and the area is very small. It is not a factory, but the outside world has rumored that a new factory has been set up. As for the report that the press's publishing house on Qipan Street will resume business as usual on the first of next month, it is even more untrue. In short, the issue of the resumption of business of the press cannot be discussed at present.

Citizens Should Prevent Cholera as Soon as Possible 126

▲Municipal Health Bureau Advises to Get Vaccinated Quickly According to the Municipal Health Bureau, cholera patients have been found in the city on April 26. It should be noted that in recent years, there has been no cholera outbreak in the city in April. Therefore, the bureau is paying close attention and sending personnel to various places to conduct thorough investigations and collect feces from suspected patients and send them to the test laboratory for testing. As of May 10, it has been tested and proven that there are already nine people suffering from cholera. Six of them live in the Public Concession, and three live in Zhabei in this city. The above nine patients are now being held in the epidemic hospital. Therefore, the bureau has already begun to implement free cholera vaccination and advised citizens to get vaccinated as soon as possible. It is said that this year the disease was discovered so early and is the most easily spread and severe infectious disease. As the saying goes, "After a great war, there must be a great epidemic." It is feared that this will be realized in the city this year, so citizens should get vaccinated to facilitate prevention.

Request to Reclaim Navigation Mark Ownership 129

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, the Joint Office of the Nine Public Shipping Companies, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and five other organizations have jointly submitted a request to the National Government's Executive Yuan and Ministry of Transportation regarding the reorganization of navigation marks on the Yangtze River, in preparation for reclaiming navigation rights in the future. Yesterday (the 11th), they jointly submitted separate petitions, requesting that the responsibility for the Yangtze River navigation marks be transferred to the Ministry for management and reorganization. The contents of the petition are excerpted below:

Presenting a petition for the reorganization of navigation marks on the Yangtze River, to facilitate transportation and safeguard sovereignty: It is noted that navigation marks are originally intended to facilitate navigation and indicate routes, and are of utmost importance to the safety of ships on the water. The navigation marks on China's Yangtze River have long been managed by the Customs Service. However, over time, this has become a mere formality. The existing facilities are incomplete, and the authority to manage these marks is in the hands of foreigners in the Customs Service, who are isolated from the situation of China's shipping industry and cannot be expected to improve it. The circumstances are detailed below for your review:

(1) The Customs Service manages the Yangtze River navigation marks by establishing a River Patrol Office, employing foreigners to fill positions. However, some of these foreigners are not familiar with river and sea conditions and are merely filling positions without competence. Technically unqualified, the various navigation marks they have established are often impractical. In this era of advancing science and technology, with daily improvements in equipment, the Customs Service has made no new investments in Yangtze River navigation marks. Even the navigation marks in inland ports along the river have not been increased to this day, leaving shipping merchants with only the obligation to pay ship dues, without enjoying the benefits of navigation.

(2) Navigation marks serve navigation, having a close relationship with pilots. However, since the Customs Service's River Patrol Office and other personnel are foreign nationals, they are detached from Chinese personnel, leading to frequent communication barriers and preventing cooperation with pilots to improve navigation. Moreover, foreign Customs officials often disregard the interests of Chinese shipping businesses, focusing solely on expanding their authority and controlling maritime administration.

(3) The Customs Service collects millions in tonnage dues from steamships annually for managing navigation marks. However, foreign staff waste expenses, with no tangible results. They have only installed a small number of lighthouses, lightships, and light buoys along the river, neglecting critical tasks such as charting the river's flow, water levels, and sectional maps. Recently, ship accidents and groundings have frequently occurred, causing passengers to feel insecure and fearful, significantly impacting the future of the shipping industry.

(4) Our treaties state that consuls should negotiate with major trading areas regarding the establishment of towers and markers to indicate navigation routes along the coast. The Yangtze River, however, is an inland waterway. Treaties between China and Britain and China and Japan only permit ships of those countries to navigate the river and do not include provisions for establishing navigation marks or management by the Customs Service along the river. The Customs Service has managed Yangtze River navigation marks for decades, effectively relinquishing sovereignty to an extreme degree. Navigation marks are a matter of transportation administration, while the Customs Service is a tax collection agency. The National Government has established a Navigation Administration Department under the Ministry of Transportation, which is responsible for the establishment and management of navigation marks. Therefore, the responsibility should be reclaimed for self-management and reorganization.

Based on the above reasons, the Yangtze River navigation marks are a matter of national sovereignty. The fact that the Customs Service has managed them for years represents a loss of authority and has produced unimpressive results. At this time of national construction and comprehensive reform, we earnestly request that your esteemed Executive Yuan and relevant ministries consider public opinion, transfer the management of these marks to the Ministry of Transportation, and order active reorganization, improve navigation facilities, and increase the number of navigation marks in inland ports. This will facilitate cooperation between shipping merchants and pilots, jointly promote the development of the shipping industry and ensure the safety of water transportation. Whether this is appropriate, we hereby respectfully submit this petition to the Chairman of the National Government, Lin, the Premier of the Executive Yuan, Wang, and the Minister of Transportation, Chen, for your review and implementation, which would be in the public interest.

Jing'an Temple on Bathing the Buddha Festival 133

Tomorrow (the 13th) is the eighth day of the fourth lunar month, traditionally known as the Bathing the Buddha Festival, which marks the birth of the Buddha Sakyamuni. Jing'an Temple, a famous ancient temple in Shanghai, holds a grand temple fair every year on this festival. Men and women, old and young, from hundreds of miles around, flock to the temple in an endless stream to offer incense and worship, crowding shoulder to shoulder. Its grandeur far surpasses that of Putuo and Lingyin. As a result, small vendors from the surrounding villages compete to set up stalls here to sell handicrafts. The roads around the temple are extremely crowded.

Last year, the Municipal Council issued a notice to ban street vendors. After the temple's abbot, Zhi Fa, vigorously negotiated, both parties finally reached an agreement, designating specific locations for vendors, thereby expanding the scope. Therefore, there are even more vendors this year. On Jing'an Temple Road, Hart Road, Haig Road, Avenue Road, Yuyuan Road, Jiaozhou Road, and Jessfield Road, there are no less than three thousand stalls. The items sold are mostly woodware, bamboo ware, rattan ware, pottery, cotton thread products, and toys. Both Chinese and foreigners enjoy buying them, as they are souvenirs filled with the essence of Chinese culture, sold in a temple fair that has been passed down for thousands of years in China.

The stallholders are grateful for Abbot Zhi Fa's efforts in negotiation and protection and plan to jointly contribute funds to send the temple a souvenir. They also plan to decorate the outside of the temple with lanterns and colored streamers and build a pine and cypress archway to enhance its beauty. However, Zhi Fa believes that because the country is in trouble, the people are suffering, and the Shanghai market has not yet recovered, the temple should not be extravagant. Moreover, the temple has established a refugee shelter, housing more than two thousand refugees, relying entirely on private donations from benefactors and receiving no assistance from other large charitable organizations. Now that the peace agreement has been signed and the Bathing the Buddha Festival is approaching, the refugees had to be given money and rice a few days before the festival and sent away to facilitate the cleaning of the halls so that worshipers from all directions could offer incense and worship. Although there are still about two hundred refugees left in the temple, every time the departed are thought of, they are alone and without homes to return to, causing tears to flow. Therefore, wasteful spending is particularly unbearable.

For this reason, the temple is not as decorated as in previous years but is open to all, allowing people to contribute as they wish and providing tea and vegetarian snacks to benefactors. Anyone wishing to study the grand occasion of Shanghai's Bathing the Buddha Festival must visit Jing'an Temple. Opium Public Sale in Progress.

(To the recipients, according to a joint letter from 20 stores, including Yu Hengchang Silk Cloth Store, located in the area of ​​the intersection of Minquan Road and Huacheng Road, the losses suffered by our stores since the outbreak of the war in Shanghai were not small. Although our location is within the concession, it happens to be outside the iron gate. During the January 28 Incident, the entire city went on strike. Although we reluctantly reopened, no customers patronized us every day. The reason is that the iron gate is closed, traffic is cut off, and customers cannot enter or exit. It is understood that places such as Nanyang Bridge and Pishao Nai Road on the border between China and France have been opened. The iron gate at the intersection of Huacheng Road, where we are located, is still closed. According to this, the current situation has calmed down, and the above-mentioned articles stated by the commercial firms are necessary for opening the iron gates. For this reason, we have written a special letter to inform you, hoping that the General Inspector will review and approve it quickly to have the iron gates at Huasheng Road Minquan Road and Route Lafayette and Route Lamber opened on the same day to facilitate traffic and promote the market, to be an indication of public interest. This is respectfully submitted to the French General Inspectorate and General Director Faber, Nanyang Bridge Commercial Federation, May 11.)

Qinghua Alumni Fete President Mei 136

The Shanghai Qinghua Alumni Association held a banquet at the Bank Association the night before yesterday in honor of Qinghua President Mei Yiqi and Ren Duyong, an executive of the China Education and Culture Foundation. Association President Cai Jinping presided over the event, and Sichuan entrepreneur Lu Zuofu was specially invited to give a lecture, which was recorded by Yang Bingxun. He stated that Sichuan's enterprises can be divided into three types: economic, security, and cultural.

Economically, the Minsheng Company is the main body. When it was founded, its capital was only 8,000 yuan, but now it has 550,000 yuan. The company focuses on shipping, power plants, coal mines, and the implementation of cooperative systems.

In terms of security, Sichuan has never experienced natural disasters, and the people have considerable self-defense capabilities. However, banditry is rampant in various places, and even the army cannot easily pass through. In the past one or two years, most of the bandits have been eliminated. The most important task now is to transform soldiers into civilians so that retired soldiers have considerable employment opportunities.

Culturally, there is the establishment of the Northwest Academy of Sciences, which focuses on the investigation of coal and iron in Sichuan and the training of accounting, secretarial, statistical, and management talents.

Finally, he said that although Sichuan's enterprise development often encounters difficulties, there are no roads that are impassable. Fang Dong

Dahua Evening News Sued 138

Since the Japanese invasion of Zhabei on January 28, public opinion and political propaganda newspapers and periodicals in Shanghai have sprung up like bamboo shoots after rain. It has now been discovered by the French Concession Police Department's Political Department that the Dahua Evening News, founded by a certain politician, contains fierce language and is mostly reactionary text attacking the government, which violates the regulations. It was discovered that the newspaper's editorial department is located at No. 6 Huabao Lane, Lage Lane, with Luo Gusun from Henan serving as the editor-in-chief, and that it is printed by the Qinye Printing House, which is located at No. 82 Gloc Road and opened by Fan Fuzhi. Therefore, at 9 pm the night before last, the detectives went to the printing house, arrested Fan, and seized 1,000 copies of the Dahua Evening News (May 9) and two plates of the day's lead type. At 11 pm, they went to the editorial department, arrested Luo Gusun, and seized 18 copies of the newspaper and a large package of letters and manuscripts, which were brought to the police station together. Yesterday, they were sent to the Fourth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, explained the case, stating that the defendants published a reactionary newspaper, and now they are being prosecuted in accordance with Articles 7, 13, 19, and 35 of the Publication Law and the various points stipulated in the French Consul's Order No. 187, requesting an investigation and submitting the newspaper as evidence. When the defendants were interrogated, they admitted to running the newspaper and printing it but denied being reactionary. A lawyer was hired to defend them. After reviewing the statements, the court announced that the hearing would be continued at a later date.

Pudong Property Dispute Murder Case 139

▲ Zhang Qingxiang Denies Killing Brother ▲ Claims Culprit is Someone Else

Zhang Qingxiang, from Huayuan Shiqiao in Pudong, and his maternal uncle, Zhang Quansheng, and his mother, Zhang Zhang, were prosecuted for murdering his biological brother, Zhang Yuxiang, and injuring his half-brother, Zhang Guoxiang, over an inheritance. The District Court's investigation determined the facts, and Zhang Qingxiang, Zhang Quansheng, and Zhang Zhang were publicly prosecuted for murder. A handgun that Zhang Quansheng had burned was also seized as evidence.

The defendant's side hired many lawyers to defend, absolutely denying the matter and saying that although Zhang Yuxiang was shot and killed, the murderer was someone else. The gun scars on Zhang Guoxiang's neck were claimed to be scrofula. However, the court's forensic doctor had examined them and the Baolong Hospital had taken photos to prove them. In order to be as detailed as possible, the court continued the trial yesterday morning, presided over by Judge Shen, and summoned Huang Rongzeng, a doctor from Baolong Hospital, to testify that Zhang Guoxiang was indeed shot at the time and that the scars were caused by surgery to remove the bullets. Liu Chen, Zhang Guoxiang's landlady, also testified in court, saying that one minute before the incident, Qingxiang came to her house to ask where Zhang Guoxiang had gone and what his housemates knew. However, Zhang Zhang and Zhang Jiayi, the owner of the shoe store, witnesses for Zhang Qingxiang, stated that Qingxiang was buying shoes that night. Because more witnesses needed to be summoned, the court ordered another hearing and remanded the defendants in custody. A famous gangster in the Xinzha district.

Record of Li Lantian's Trial 140

Among the 59 male and female suspects in the large number of theft cases successively apprehended by the Xinzha Police Department a month ago, 36 who were found to be unrelated were released by the First Special District Court after investigation. The remaining 21 men, including Sun Honggui, Wang Zixiang, Xin Fayu, Lu Ruicheng, Han Xiaolong, Sun Qiyou, Lin Shihua, Gu Zhiheng, Mao Laohu, Yang Yongsheng, Xu Maokun, Xu Yueming, Gong Sangong, Li Lantian, Cao Zilin, Ding Xiaodi, Qi Zengfu, Shen Tongnan, Wang Yinfu, Yang Agen, and Wang Zaiqiu, and the two women, Wang Zhang and Wang Quan, were still detained for trial. The details have been recorded in the newspapers many times.

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide continued the trial, with defense attorneys Fan Gang, E Sen, Jiang Yiping, Shan Yuhua, and Bao Zhenhuang, as well as police attorney Wang Yaotang, attending successively. Judge Feng still ordered the individual interrogation of the defendants for each of the charged cases.

The police attorney stated that after investigation, Sun Honggui was found to have committed other robbery cases with Deng Youcai. Deng was also arrested, but his case is being heard by Judge Wu Tingqi. It is requested that Sun's case be combined into that case and also be heard by Judge Wu to avoid discrepancies. Judge Feng approved the request and ordered the police to take Sun away.

Li Lantian was then brought to the case. The police attorney stated that Li is a famous gangster in the Xinzha district. For the past few years, he has specialized in extortion, and the merchants in the district have mostly been victimized by him. The police have long wanted to arrest him, but because his gang is very large and well-informed, it is difficult to catch him. After his arrest this time, it was discovered that on July 28 of last year, Xu Wang and Wang Xu, sisters-in-law residing on Shanhai Road, had a quarrel and each hired gangsters to go to Xiyuan on Xinzha Road to have tea. In one case, a gangster fired three shots in a row, and Li was on guard at the scene. Furthermore, on the morning of March 17 of this year, there was a case of gangsters firing guns along the way on Xizang Road, and Li was also involved. A strict investigation should be requested. The Western Detective also reported that after Li was arrested this time, merchants in the district reported various illegal acts he had committed and demanded punishment. Cai Xinghe, a waiter at Xiyuan Teahouse, testified that Wang Xu and others hired people to drink tea and that the gangsters fired guns. However, he said that Li was not at the scene that day. Although Wang Xu and others were also summoned, they denied drinking tea and shooting. When questioned, Li Lantian claimed that he had been a detective in the Kunshan County Public Security Bureau since March of last year. He denied all the alleged cases. Judge Feng then ordered Xin Fayu, Lu Ruicheng, Han Xiaolong, and others to be questioned about the circumstances of the case in which they ganged up with weapons to rob the Dai Chunlin Perfumery on Xinzha Road of banknotes and foreign money on October 23 of the 19th year. By the time the interrogation was over, it was dusk, so the judge ordered that the defendants remain in custody and adjourned the hearing.

Opinions on Tutelage and Constitutionalism 146

By Wang Zaoshi - A critique of the speeches of Wang Jingwei and Yu Youren

Since some of the invited members of the National Crisis Conference put forward the proposal to end party rule and implement democracy, the issue of tutelage versus constitutionalism has gradually attracted serious attention in society. Kuomintang leaders such as Wang Jingwei, Hu Hanmin, Sun Ke, and Yu Youren have all expressed their opinions. Wang and Yu oppose ending tutelage, while Sun supports it. Hu's attitude is unclear. As someone who studies politics and advocates for ending tutelage and implementing constitutionalism, I cannot help but offer my humble opinion on this important issue.

The reasons why Wang and Yu oppose ending tutelage can be analyzed into four points: (1) They believe that the Chinese people are too uneducated to practice democracy and implement constitutionalism without the Kuomintang's tutelage. (2) They believe that without the Kuomintang, there would be no Republic of China; destroying tutelage would be destroying the Kuomintang; and destroying the Kuomintang would be destroying the Republic of China. (3) They believe that past constitutionalism had poor results, so constitutionalism should not be implemented now. (4) They believe that some of the people advocating for constitutionalism now are former (bureaucratic politicians) who are not qualified to talk about party politics.

First, let's discuss the first reason for opposing the end of tutelage: the belief that the Chinese people are too uneducated to practice democracy and implement constitutionalism without the Kuomintang's tutelage. This reason must be based on at least the following foundations to be self-consistent: (1) The Kuomintang itself is sound. (2) The Kuomintang members are the best and brightest in the country. (3) The Kuomintang has had great achievements in the past. If the Kuomintang itself is divided and lacks a whole party organization, party will, and party policy, how can it "tutor"? If the Kuomintang itself is full of new and old bureaucratic politicians and warlords, not only are they not the best and brightest in the country, but many are even social outcasts, then how can they "tutor"? If five years of tutelage has led to the loss of sovereignty and national humiliation, endless internal strife, bandits everywhere, and corrupt officials throughout the country, bringing the nation to the brink of collapse and the people to the brink of starvation, how can we continue to "tutor" like this? These are objective facts that cannot be denied or concealed. Whether the Kuomintang can tutor and should continue to tutor depends on whether it possesses the above three conditions; otherwise, the Kuomintang is not qualified to talk about tutelage and should end tutelage.

The fundamental theory of tutelage originates from "rule by the wise," which should be carried out by the "wise" tutoring the "unworthy" and by a minority ruling the majority. But who are the "wise" among those few, and who are the "unworthy" among those many? This is a question that proponents of aristocratic politics in the past and proponents of the tutelage system today cannot answer. The theory of aristocratic politics failed here, and the theory of tutelage politics also fails here. Aristocratic politics is a political system in which a minority wields political power and most citizens have no opportunity to participate in politics. Therefore, the Kuomintang's tutelage today can also be said to be a form of aristocratic politics. Some proponents of aristocratic politics base it on bloodline, saying that a minority of hereditary aristocrats should rule the majority of commoners, but the children of aristocratic families are often ignorant young masters. Some base it on wealth, saying that a minority of wealthy people should rule the majority of poor people, but the wealthy do not necessarily have political ability. Some base it on knowledge, saying that a minority of people with higher education should rule the majority of uneducated people, but many in the intellectual class are mere bookworms. Now, may I ask what the Kuomintang's tutelage-style aristocratic politics is based on? It is not based on bloodline, nor on wealth, nor on education, but in name on party membership, and in reality subordinate to warlords. If we say that all Kuomintang members are the wise, the best in the country, the first to know and perceive, and should be the ruling class; if we say that all non-Kuomintang members are the unworthy, the last to know and perceive, and should be ruled slaves, then this "aristocratic" standard is too unreasonable. Moreover, the facts tell us that many Kuomintang members today are not outstanding in terms of personality, knowledge, or talent.

The above are the reasons why the Kuomintang cannot "tutor" and is not qualified to "tutor." Even assuming that the Kuomintang can "tutor" and is qualified to "tutor," political history tells us that talking about tutelage makes it impossible to talk about democracy. First, it is theoretically inconsistent. If there is a tutelage ruling class and a tutored ruled class, Wang still says that he can "cultivate civil rights" and that "the people's power is increasing day by day in time and expanding day by day in space." This is a lie. The development of civil rights must be automatic; if it is "tutored" out, it is not civil rights. Looking through the history of various countries in the world, may I ask which country's democracy was "tutored" by the rulers? May I also ask which country's democracy was not won by the people? Second, it is factually inconsistent. Any individual or group that obtains political power and occupies a ruling position is always unwilling to let go. This is a universal human trait. The political history of all countries can prove this. The tutelage theory hopes that the tutelage ruling class will train the general public to seize the political power they monopolize and transition from tutelage to constitutionalism, which is also deception. What was the Kuomintang's tutelage like in the past? The Kuomintang's tutelage will probably be the same in the future. Not to mention others, Wang and Yu are the first to seize political power and not let go. Therefore, talking about tutelage makes it impossible to talk about democracy; talking about democracy requires opposing tutelage. The two cannot be combined; Wang and Yu should choose for themselves.

The second reason for opposing the end of tutelage is that without the Kuomintang, there would be no Republic of China; destroying tutelage would be destroying the Kuomintang; and destroying the Kuomintang would be destroying the Republic of China. This is not only illogical but also intentionally insulting to the people of the whole country. Let's break it down and discuss whether there would be no Republic of China without the Kuomintang. The birth of the Republic of China was caused by many factors, such as the intrusion of Western culture, the oppression of foreign powers, the corruption of the Qing Dynasty, and the impact of the industrial revolution. These were the fundamental causes of the revolution. Even in terms of overthrowing the rule of the Manchus, many individuals and groups other than the Kuomintang made contributions. Now, Wang and Yu are dismissing this with a single stroke of the pen, which is either due to ignorance or intentional exaggeration. Generally speaking, a revolution in a country must have fundamental causes; as long as the fundamental conditions are ripe, the revolutionary party is just happening to be there at the right time. If the Kuomintang had not carried out the Xinhai Revolution, someone else would have. Moreover, the revolution against the Manchus was not carried out by the Kuomintang alone, and it was certainly not carried out by the current Kuomintang. The main force in overthrowing Yuan Shikai was Cai E and others, not the Kuomintang. Furthermore, the current peril of the Republic of China is largely the responsibility of the current Kuomintang members. Now that foreign enemies have invaded the country, the ruling Kuomintang leaders, such as Wang and Yu, should apologize to the people of the whole country instead of saying that without the Kuomintang, there would be no Republic of China. That is simply outrageous!

As for whether destroying tutelage means destroying the Kuomintang, it is not difficult to answer if we look at the party politics of democratic countries. Political parties do not necessarily need tutelage; abolishing tutelage does not mean abolishing the party that advocates tutelage. The Kuomintang was a party before tutelage, and it will still be a party even if tutelage ends now. The reason why we advocate ending tutelage is only to abolish the Kuomintang's special position of monopolizing political power. From one perspective, it is not destroying the Kuomintang but trying to preserve the Kuomintang's political life and prevent it from being overthrown by revolution.

As for saying that destroying the Kuomintang means destroying the Republic of China, that is even more ridiculous. The Republic of China is not a parasite of the Kuomintang; on the contrary, the Kuomintang is a parasite of the Republic of China. If the Kuomintang is eliminated, the Republic of China will not necessarily be eliminated; if the Republic of China is eliminated, the Kuomintang will inevitably be eliminated. As the saying goes, "When the skin is gone, what will the hair cling to?" Moreover, given how the Kuomintang has been acting in recent years, losing sovereignty and national humiliation externally, oppressing the people internally, putting the party above the country, and having a party but no country, even if it comes to the point where the Kuomintang's political power is abolished, it may not be a bad way to support the Republic of China. (To be continued)
